  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e02cf584-bd50-4d69-a03c-319c5f7d9c59'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10737922967220696296">In the 1890s Conor and his family live on the sovereign Saltee Islands, off the Irish coast. Conor spends his days studying the science of flight with his tutor and exploring the castle with the king’s daughter, Princess Isabella. But the boy’s idyllic life changes forever the day he discovers a deadly conspiracy against the king. When Conor tries to intervene, he is brand</span>
  <span id="freeText10737922967220696296" style="display:none">In the 1890s Conor and his family live on the sovereign Saltee Islands, off the Irish coast. Conor spends his days studying the science of flight with his tutor and exploring the castle with the king’s daughter, Princess Isabella. But the boy’s idyllic life changes forever the day he discovers a deadly conspiracy against the king. When Conor tries to intervene, he is branded a traitor and thrown into jail on the prison island of Little Saltee. There, he has to fight for his life, as he and the other prisoners are forced to mine for diamonds in inhumane conditions.<br /><br />There is only one way to escape Little Saltee, and that is to fly. So Conor passes the solitary months by scratching drawings of flying machines on the prison walls. The months turn into years; but eventually the day comes when Conor must find the courage to trust his revolutionary designs and take to the air.<br /></span>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_12912445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12912445" />
    <a title="Betsy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221050-betsy"><img alt="Betsy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442631153p2/221050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12912445?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy" href="/user/show/221050-betsy">Betsy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12912445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17437866981260315102">How Not to Review a Book: Do not begin your review by jumping off into some big old rant about how you never liked anything the author wrote before, particularly if you are about to praise their newest novel. Do not use phrases like “how did this happen?” and “why now?” and “are they near death?” You may mention how impressed you were with the author’s speaking engagements, mentioning in passing their brilliant encapsulation of, oh say, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227866.The_Legend_of_Spud_Murphy' title='The Legend of Spud Murphy by Eoin Colfer' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Legend of Spud Murphy</a>. Do not then mention how disappo</span>
  <span id="freeText17437866981260315102" style="display:none">How Not to Review a Book: Do not begin your review by jumping off into some big old rant about how you never liked anything the author wrote before, particularly if you are about to praise their newest novel. Do not use phrases like “how did this happen?” and “why now?” and “are they near death?” You may mention how impressed you were with the author’s speaking engagements, mentioning in passing their brilliant encapsulation of, oh say, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227866.The_Legend_of_Spud_Murphy" title="The Legend of Spud Murphy by Eoin Colfer" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Legend of Spud Murphy</a>. Do not then mention how disappointed you were in the book itself and how you always wished they’d live up to that brilliant potential palpable in person. Don’t do any of that. It’ll just get your review off to a bad start and put all those <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/249747.Artemis_Fowl__Artemis_Fowl___1_" title="Artemis Fowl (Artemis Fowl, #1) by Eoin Colfer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Artemis Fowl</a> fans on the defensive (for example). If you’re going to write a review of a book that you loved, adored, swallowed whole and digested with relish, DO begin your review that way. Catharsis has not place in professional book review circles. Not the nice ones, anyway.<br />	<br />Yes, ladies and gentlemen, that roundabout little introduction is just my way of saying how much I loved <i>Airman</i>. It was one of those books I saw sitting on my boss’s bookshelf that made me think, “Maybe I should read that.” It wasn’t until multiple people told me in person and repeatedly how good it was that I caved. And it really is good, gentle reader. It puts the buckle in swashbuckling. The play in swordplay. The terror in terrific. It's a good old-fashioned tale of thwarted romance, betrayal, great heroism, murder, diamonds, villains, kings, Americans, thugs, and a boy with the unusual inclination to fly.<br /><br />The thing to know about Conor Broekhart, before all the nastiness occurred, was that he was born in the sky. A hot air balloon, if you wanted me to be more precise. A falling, soon-to-be-crushed, death trap of a balloon, to be even closer to the mark. Of course Conor didn't die, and as a result his family returned to their home on the Saltee Islands (just off the coast of Ireland) with a new baby to introduce to the King. Conor's father was the king's right hand man, and because they were so close the boy grew up running around the castle with his best friend, the princess. But that was before the king was murdered. Before Conor was thrown into jail on the Little Saltee island (think Alcatraz, but with less charm). Before the boy discovered how to survive in his new, harsh, surroundings and find a way out of his predicament. And now the princess and his family are in mortal peril, unless Conor can truly crack the riddle of how to construct a machine that will fly.<br /><br />Is it fantasy? No more than any historical novel where the hero indulges in science. Is it science fiction? Only if you consider the notion of one man discovering the use of propellers on his own fantastical. Is it steampunk? No. Stop being silly. No this is, odd as it may sound, fiction with spice. That's not really a category, so I don't know if you can call it anything but original. Frances Hardinge's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/710437.Fly_by_Night__Fly_by_Night___1_" title="Fly by Night (Fly by Night, #1) by Frances Hardinge" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fly by Night</a> suffered similar categorical problems. Her book seemed like a fantasy, but like this book it was merely an alternate history. Still, if lumping this puppy in with 500+ page fantasy tomes is the only way to get kids to read it, so be it. I've no objections on my end.<br /><br />For all its 416 pages, the book feels very tight. Colfer keeps a firm hand on the reins of his plot, never indulging too far in one direction or another. The result is a story that flies by with hardly a gasp for breath. This isn't to say that the author doesn't indulge in a small aside once in a while. He does, but they're always very quick and funny. For example, when the castle tower is on fire and King Nicholas must escape from his royal bathroom the text reads, "There was a window, of course. Nicholas was a great believer in the benefits of good ventilation. He was a devotee of meditation, too; but this was hardly the time for it."<br /><br />There are also copious details that give the book just enough heft to keep it from feeling too frivolous. They tend to be little things. The scrape of the bolt on prison doors is described as "Top C", with the side note, "Social diarists record that survivors of Little Saltee often suffered from insomnia unless their bedchamber doors were fitted with rusted bolts." There are references to Napoleon's stay at Little Saltee (apparently he fared poorly). I liked the little mites that eat away the disease and filth from new prisoners. And Conor's method of writing down his schematics is probably the closest this book comes to science fiction, without ever really treading fully down that path.<br /><br />Kids looking for excitement will find it from page one onward. And yet, for all its death-defying escapades, Colfer is very careful to cover his bases. He doesn't get sloppy on the details. By the end of the book the reasons why Conor wasn't killed at the same time as Nicholas and why the princess is left living are explained perfectly without so much as a glint of a gap in sight. Kids will enjoy the book because the characters are great and the story is fun. Adults will enjoy it because it won't require extraordinary suspensions of disbelief. Plus the fact that this is a stand-alone novel that does not lend itself naturally to sequels or a series is like a palate cleanser in this sequel-addled age with live in.<br /><br />Colfer shows himself to be a skillful writer by his interesting choices. Under normal circumstances, when the hero in a story has a plan and doesn't let the reader in on it, usually that plan goes off without a hitch. It doesn't look as if Colfer understood that concept, though, and the book is stronger for it. He also must have never heard the rule that the more often the hero is knocked unconscious, the worse the book is. Conor gets his own fair share of blows to the head, but the author always plays fair and never uses that as an excuse to fudge details or bridge insurmountable distances. Well played.<br /><br />I also had great respect for Colfer when he saw to it that his hero never became a murderer. Our heroes in movies and books like killing henchmen. The idea that an action packed storyline requires that your protagonist have blood on his hands is a complex issue, too easily skirted around. Colfer isn't afraid to face the problem head-on, though, making it perfectly clear that the "kill or be killed" mode of thought only means that under the right circumstances it is the people without the proper intelligence or imagination who are the ones who descend into becoming killers.<br /><br />And on a personal note, I was happy to see that the Yanks in this book come off looking pretty good. Good King Nicholas, the forward thinking monarch on the Saltee throne, is an American. Linus Wynter, the kind blind prisoner who helps Conor survive prison, is also an American. We haven't looked this good on paper since Lee Scoresby first showed his face in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials___1_" title="The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, #1) by Philip Pullman" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Golden Compass</a>.<br /><br />Some people say the book is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7126.The_Count_of_Monte_Cristo" title="The Count of Monte Cristo by Alexandre Dumas" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Count of Monte Cristo</a>. Others argue that it feels more like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54499.The_Man_in_the_Iron_Mask__The_D_Artagnan_Romances___3_3_" title="The Man in the Iron Mask (The D'Artagnan Romances, #3.3) by Alexandre Dumas" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Man in the Iron Mask</a>. With such esteemed comparisons, it shouldn't hurt matters any to also note that it also happens to be consistently interesting, smart, exciting, and fun. The finest book Eoin Colfer has ever written, and hopefully the start of more stories like this to come. Everyone should read it. <br /><br />For ages 8-15.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17437866981260315102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147480017" />
    <a title="Stephanie (Bookfever)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4939266-stephanie-bookfever"><img alt="Stephanie (Bookfever)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595589358p2/4939266.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141322216" href="/book/show/6333622-airman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=owned-physical-books">owned-physical-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147480017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8643416881913329002"><b>NEW EDITION OF AIRMAN COMING MARCH 2, 2021 BY DISNEY-HYPERION</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Airman is a very special book to me. I read it a few times when I was younger and I thought it was high time for a re-read. I'm so glad to find it even better than I remembered. As much as I love Eoin Colfer's Artemis Fowl series, I have to say that I think Airman is his best work so far (of the books I have read by him). It's simply a beautiful story. I'd forgotten how beautiful it really was. It also has a lot of adventure, a budding</span>
  <span id="freeText8643416881913329002" style="display:none"><b>NEW EDITION OF AIRMAN COMING MARCH 2, 2021 BY DISNEY-HYPERION</b><br /><br /><br /><br />Airman is a very special book to me. I read it a few times when I was younger and I thought it was high time for a re-read. I'm so glad to find it even better than I remembered. As much as I love Eoin Colfer's Artemis Fowl series, I have to say that I think Airman is his best work so far (of the books I have read by him). It's simply a beautiful story. I'd forgotten how beautiful it really was. It also has a lot of adventure, a budding romance that I adored and some the most unique characters I have ever read about. <br /><br />I am not kidding, this book has the best set of characters ever. How could someone forget about characters like the Victor 'La Brosse' Vigny, King Nicholas, Linus Wynter, Princess/Queen Isabella or Conor Broekhart himself and his parents, Declan and Catherine? Even little Sean Broekhart! They were all amazing. And as per usual with Eoin Colfer, we get a despicable villain who is just loathsome. Together with the story devided in three parts: Broekhart - Finn - Airman, it's just all part of Eoin Colfer's genius. I loved this book before but I love it even more now after re-reading it.<br /><br />I also have to say that I had a lot of emotional moments with this book. Conor goes through a whole lot of crap, going to prison because of that bastard Bonvilain and some parts really did bring tears to my eyes. So this book has been a rollercoaster of emotions but it was totally worth it. I was also rather giddy when Otto Malarkey came into the picture because he's also in The Reluctant Assassin. I just love Eoin Colfer for that. That and his totally amazing and awesome writing!<br /><br />So what else can I say but that I love Airman? I've always thought Artemis Fowl was by favorite book by him but I think I'll have to put Airman in that place now because... simply wow! Mr. Colfer has once again left me awe-struck with his amazing book, Airman!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8643416881913329002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1370674551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1370674551" />
    <a title="Hope" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30387463-hope"><img alt="Hope" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568050992p2/30387463.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1370674551?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hope" href="/user/show/30387463-hope">Hope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30387463-hope?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30387463-hope?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30387463-hope?shelf=action-and-adventure">action-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30387463-hope?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1370674551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3813517620516518953">"Airman" is the thrilling story of a fourteen year old boy named Conor Broekhart who dreams of flight. Unfortunately, his dreams are dashed when Conor is accused of murdering the king and is sent to the dreaded prison island of Little Saltee. All throughout his stay, Conor draws up his plans of escape, but the only way to escape Little Saltee is to fly. <br/><br/>I loved Conor Broekhart so much. He was this sweet, innocent, and nerdy kid who was obsessed with planes and gliders and such. I loved getting t</span>
  <span id="freeText3813517620516518953" style="display:none">"Airman" is the thrilling story of a fourteen year old boy named Conor Broekhart who dreams of flight. Unfortunately, his dreams are dashed when Conor is accused of murdering the king and is sent to the dreaded prison island of Little Saltee. All throughout his stay, Conor draws up his plans of escape, but the only way to escape Little Saltee is to fly. <br /><br />I loved Conor Broekhart so much. He was this sweet, innocent, and nerdy kid who was obsessed with planes and gliders and such. I loved getting to read about little Conor at the beginning and seeing how much he grows and changes throughout the book. And I also loved seeing how he dealt with his crush on Isabella. *snickers* <br /><br />I must warn you that this book gets a bit dark. During his stay at Little Saltee, Conor changes. There's this part where I almost put the book down. Don't. It gets so much better. It almost broke my heart when he almost carried out his foul deed. But he didn't. #spoilers There are also a few parts where I was a bit horrified by the violence, though. *nods* Yeah. <br /><br />The beginning, to me, was a bit boring. At first, I didn't quite understand how this tied in to the rest of the story, but as the story went on, it got really good. It takes a little while for the book to get started, but once it does, it goes quite fast. <br /><br />It seemed like the story jumped around a bit. I would have liked it if the author focused on a few parts more than others, but oh well. <br /><br />I wasn't a huge fan of the last chapter. It just . . . I dunno. I thought it was kind of unnecessary. *shrugs* <br /><br />All in all, this book was great. I loved the characters, the plot, and the fast paced-ness. I would totally recommend this book to anyone and everyone who loves a good, adventurous story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3813517620516518953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9990814799068864829"><b>February 13-14, 2019</b><br/><br/>Has it really been that long since I read this book? Sad! It's sooooo good! I went to my 3rd grader's book fair, which was in their school library, and saw this on the shelf. I was like, "Yaaaasss I want to read it again!!!"   <span id="freeText9990814799068864829" style="display:none"><b>February 13-14, 2019</b><br /><br />Has it really been that long since I read this book? Sad! It's sooooo good! I went to my 3rd grader's book fair, which was in their school library, and saw this on the shelf. I was like, "Yaaaasss I want to read it again!!!" So I did. :) What a great book!!<br /><br /><b>November 1-3, 2013</b><br /><br />Only 42 stars, Past Sara? Really? I know you were trying to be funny with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy___1_" title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Hitchhiker's</a> reference there, but you were seriously undervaluing this book!<br /><br />It's AWESOME. Conor is THE BEST EVAR!!! It's kind of a teenage boy book, as it's about a teenage boy, but whatever! Eoin Colfer's Artemis Fowl books are really great, but this is my favorite of all his books!<br /><br />The audiobook is really great, too! LOVE IT!!!!!! <br /><br /><b>August 25-27, 2010</b><br /><br />Fabulous the second time around, too! :)<br /><br /><b>November 9, 2008</b><br /><br />If I could give it 42 stars, I would.<br /><br />Ahhhhh!!!! It was SOOO SOOOOOOO SOOOOOOOOOO GOOD!!! Seriously... listening to it in the car probably wasn't safe, as periodically, I would slam the steering wheel in frustration or anticipation and yell, "HOLY FREAKING CRAP!!!" It was SOOOOOOO EXCITING!!! I loved it. (And of course I did.... it is "recommended to listeners ages 12 to 17"... durrrrr...)<br /><br />It ended so well! *giggly-happy sigh* :)<br /><br />Okay, so I suppose you want to know what it's about, eh? Well, it's about this kid, Conor Broekhart (Irish), who is 15 (after the prologue, which tells about how he was born in a hot-air balloon), who dreams of flying. He lives on a little island called Great Saltee. His father, mother, and he are close friends with the King and his daughter, Isabella. (Side note: I'm surprised to say, hearing her name NEVER reminded me of Bella (Twilight)! Shocking!) He kinda becomes sidekick to the royal scientist.<br /><br />I don't want to get into too much detail, but I'll write what's on the back of the CD:<br /><br />"Conor spends his days studying the science of flight with his tutor and exploring the castle with the king's daughter, Princess Isabella [who routinely threatens to have him hanged... :)]. But the boy's idyllic life changes forever the day he discovers a deadly conspiracy against the king. When Conor tries to intervene, he is branded a traitor and thrown into jail on the prison island of Little Saltee. There, he has to fight for his life, as he and the other prisoners are forced to mind for diamonds in inhumane conditions.<br /><br />"There is only one way to escape Little Saltee, and that is to fly...."<br /><br />There's more, but holy spoilers, Batman! That was bad enough!<br /><br />It was fascinating and I loved it.</span>

This book, and my feels, took a beating. There were some points when I wanted to throw it across the room and go hurt something. It's that good.<br/> I advise, before you start this book, to invest in a good psychiatrist. The plotting is so...thick...so complex that I could hardly put it down. (Unfortunately, I had to, as I had to see to my life and feed myself.) But, really, Eoin Colfer, I love you dearly. The characters, the plot, the whole world is just fantastic</span>
  <span id="freeText10564290816213080037" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380432445ra/868651.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> Wow. That's all I can really say. This book, and my feels, took a beating. There were some points when I wanted to throw it across the room and go hurt something. It's that good.<br> I advise, before you start this book, to invest in a good psychiatrist. The plotting is so...thick...so complex that I could hardly put it down. (Unfortunately, I had to, as I had to see to my life and feed myself.) But, really, Eoin Colfer, I love you dearly. The characters, the plot, the whole world is just fantastic. And, Mr. Colfer doesn't make you swim through pages of gelatinous prose. (Thank you, for that.)He's concise, descriptive, and legendary.<br> The villains are delightfully...villainous. The protagonists--and there are many--are complex, and at times, flawed. I just...I can't believe that I stumbled on this book and wasn't sure of it at first. It changed. My. Life.<br> Okay, so, as far as "adult-ish" situations go, I can't recall any, offhand. Language, a few H words, and...the D word. Violence--well, Conor is kind of beaten-up quite a few times. Nothing severely graphic. And, it's subtly steampunk, and that makes my day.<br> Basically, it's a great book if you want to be emotionally attached to a bunch of characters who get beat up on by the world. Which, I'm all for. Thank you, Eoin Colfer, I bow to you, o great entity of spectacular words!</span>

<div id="review_147602815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147602815" />
    <a title="Janette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1292612-janette"><img alt="Janette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442459284p2/1292612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147602815?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janette" href="/user/show/1292612-janette">Janette</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147602815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2731658940678494806">First of all, let me say that I am a total Eoin Colfer fan. Really. I bought this book without knowing anything about it except that Eoin Colfer wrote it--and I usually don't do that. He is such a skilled writer though. He effortlessly juggles pacing, dialogue, action, internal thought, characterization, description--all of it. He makes it look easy. And in omniscient point of view too.<br/><br/>That said, I had a major problem with this book. One part was totally unbelievable.<br/><br/>*spoiler alert*<br/><br/>Oh, I was wil</span>
  <span id="freeText2731658940678494806" style="display:none">First of all, let me say that I am a total Eoin Colfer fan. Really. I bought this book without knowing anything about it except that Eoin Colfer wrote it--and I usually don't do that. He is such a skilled writer though. He effortlessly juggles pacing, dialogue, action, internal thought, characterization, description--all of it. He makes it look easy. And in omniscient point of view too.<br /><br />That said, I had a major problem with this book. One part was totally unbelievable.<br /><br />*spoiler alert*<br /><br />Oh, I was willing to believe that Connor, as a child, could make a hang glider out of a flag and toothpicks to save himself and the princess from a burning tower. (Okay, it wasn't toothpicks, but still . . .) I was willing to believe that he could escape from prison hanging onto a basketless air balloon, and even that he was able to sit down with some local lads and put together an airplane before the Wright brothers.<br /><br />Here is the scene that had me ejecting the CD and moaning, "Why Eoin? Why would you write that?"<br /><br />Obvious villain, Hugo, has just killed a man who is not only king, but also a close friend of Connor's family. He and the princess have been friends since birth and now have romantic feelings for each other.<br /><br />Fourteen year old Connor hears the murder happen, bursts into the room and tries to stop Hugo. Hugo beats him senseless, puts him in chains and tells Connor's father that Connor has killed the king.<br /><br />Connor's father, who happens to be captain of guards, goes to see his son in prison and--get this--never even asks Connor if he did it. He doesn't listen to his obviously beaten son, say anything. Instead he yells at Connor for being a traitor and disowns him.<br /><br />What??????!!!! Come on, the kid is fourteen!<br /><br />There's absolutely no evidence that Connor has done this crime and he has no motivation for doing it.<br /><br />Any half-way decent parent would at least ask if the allegation were actually true. Even a bad parent would try to defend their child if for no other reason then they wouldn’t want to be tainted with the crime themselves. But not Connor's dad. He sends him off to a prison camp where he will be beaten some more.<br /><br />And if that isn't hard enough to believe, once Conner escapes, he harbors no ill feelings toward his father. Excuse me, my children harbor ill feelings toward me when I tell them they'll be excused from the dinner table if they don't use good table manners. (Really, I have one son who is still going on about a certain toast incident.)<br /><br />I never could really get over that aspect of the story.<br /><br />Still, it's always nice to listen to a guy with an Irish accent narrate the story. And the last Artemis Fowl book was totally awesome so I still love you, Eoin.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2731658940678494806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23015762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23015762" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/999233-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594609442p2/999233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23015762?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/999233-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=read-2008">read-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=review-on-blog">review-on-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23015762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1061558885797088736">Conor Broekhart lives on a small island governed by King Nicholas Trudeau. Conor's days are spent with his tudor and playing with princess Isabella. But Conor's real passion is flying. All Conor's life he's dreamed of flying. He spends massive amounts of time and energy pursuing his obsession. That changes when he discovers a plot to overthrow the king and becomes tangled in the mess and branded as a traitor, being sent off to work in the diamond mines on little Saltee.<br/><br/>I decided to read this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText1061558885797088736" style="display:none">Conor Broekhart lives on a small island governed by King Nicholas Trudeau. Conor's days are spent with his tudor and playing with princess Isabella. But Conor's real passion is flying. All Conor's life he's dreamed of flying. He spends massive amounts of time and energy pursuing his obsession. That changes when he discovers a plot to overthrow the king and becomes tangled in the mess and branded as a traitor, being sent off to work in the diamond mines on little Saltee.<br /><br />I decided to read this book because I saw that my friend had read it and given it 5 stars....so I was curious. I've read some of the artemis fowl books, but I wasn't impressed, and I thought that they were awfully violent. I really could have cared less about any new books Eoin Colfer had published, but I had read his Supernaturalist book and it wasn't too bad, so I decided to give this book a try. <br /> In the beginning I found the storyline to be pretty interesting, I kept reading because I wanted to know what would happen at the end, but when I finally got there, I was disappointed. I really thought it was annoying how the main character, Conor kept getting stuff thrown at him - all the time. It seemed like he could never really rest because something was about to happen, which was a little tiring for me. Even though I do approve of exciting and thrilling books, I do think that there are such things as "too much excitement" and this book crossed the line. <br /> I do know not what it is about Eoin Colfer but he always seems to include a decent amount of violence, and it really is rather unnerving. Everybody is constantly being brutally beaten up. Also, the bad guys are always BAD TO THE CORE, and Conor can usually tell what they are thinking by the look in their eyes (something I thought was unrealistic and slightly aggravating).<br /> Conor, that's another interesting aspect; I really thought that he was just a little too perfect. He was handsome, brilliant, athletic and loved by a princess - what more could he want? To me, the author describing him as such only made me like him less, I wanted someone that I could relate to. <br /> The reason this gets such a low rating is because I just could not bring myself to group it with the "three star" books, it just didn't seem quite up to par, while I thought it was an okay book without any language or adult content, I didn't enjoy it enough to recommend it to friends. I just don't really care for Eoin Colfer's writing style, his characters and the way they are portrayed just bugs me, but if you are a fan, you'd probably like this book.<br /><br />*Taken from my book reviews blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008/05/book-review-74-airman-by-eoin-colfer.html">http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1061558885797088736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_55436162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55436162" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55436162?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423107514" href="/book/show/5990018-airman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55436162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14950613501014098819">I picked this book up quite a while ago, but never got around to reading it until I decided to give it away. I'm not sure why I never read it, because everything about this seems like it would be to my taste. I really enjoyed the Artemis Fowl series, and laugh like a loon whenever I read them, so I had a pretty good idea that I would like his other books, but still I put this off. <br/><br/>Well I'm glad that I decided to give it away, because it gave me an excuse to read this sooner than later, and I'm h</span>
  <span id="freeText14950613501014098819" style="display:none">I picked this book up quite a while ago, but never got around to reading it until I decided to give it away. I'm not sure why I never read it, because everything about this seems like it would be to my taste. I really enjoyed the Artemis Fowl series, and laugh like a loon whenever I read them, so I had a pretty good idea that I would like his other books, but still I put this off. <br /><br />Well I'm glad that I decided to give it away, because it gave me an excuse to read this sooner than later, and I'm happy to say that I really enjoyed it. <br /><br />This was nothing like the AF series. There's not really any fantasy here, or magic or ridiculous jokes or gutter-humor or any of the stuff that I loved about the AF series, but I enjoyed this as much for the lack of those things as I loved AF for them. This book definitely has a more serious, somber tone, and in many ways it reminded me of one of the greats, The Count of Monte Cristo. That is a huge compliment coming from me, because COMC is without a doubt one of the greatest books about betrayal and revenge ever written, and I adored all 1300 pages of it. This is not a YA reproduction of The Count of Monte Cristo, however. The storyline here veers off in its own direction, and follows its own trail, but the tone, and some of the details just brought the classic to mind. <br /><br />I glanced at a few reviews of this book and see that a common complaint was the darkness and bleak feeling of the story, the hopelessness. I don't agree that that's how the story was portrayed. Yes, overall it was far from light and happy, but again the story warranted a darker and hopeless feeling. I thought the somber tone was appropriate for this story, considering all that poor Conor endured, and all that he lost: his freedom, his family, his love, his country, his honor. These are not happy events. Even so, Colfer did a great job at weaving some threads of lightness and humor into the story to break up the solemnity of the main story. It was done in a very subtle manner, not at all overstated and blatant like the humor in the Artemis Fowl series, but it had me giggling all the same. Anyway, what I'm trying to say is that the tone fit the story for me, and anything much lighter would have been out of place. <br /><br />Moving on to the characters, I have to say that I really liked all of them. I would have liked a little bit more depth, especially in Conor. As much as I liked him, and I really did, his only real flaw was in his despair and willingness to move on and start over without even trying to bring out the truth and set things to rights. I know that he'd been through a torturous 3 years, but considering that he was so determined in everything else, you'd think that his determination, and the anger at his mistreatment would spark a vengeance in him. He was just a little too perfect, a little too noble and charitable. <br /><br />I really liked Declan, Conor's father, and felt for his loss. He was grieving and feeling guilty and angry and lost himself. Even though I empathized with him, I still would have liked a bit more personal grief and anger from him. It was told, not felt. It served the purpose, but I would have just liked a bit more. <br /><br />The Marshall was decidedly villainous and evil, and even though I immensely disliked him, I could not help but laugh at some of his wittier comments and thoughts. He's so unabashedly bad that he becomes a bit funny, but not funny to the point at which he's no longer awful, but just funny as in "Wow, I can't believe people are really THAT horrible!"<br /><br />I really liked the scientific and engineering historical references in this story. It lent the book a feeling of realism and groundedness that it would have been lacking otherwise. I would still classify it as an adventure story, but with these details, it has a more real historical feel. <br /><br />I must admit that I was so engrossed in the story that I was surprised to find that 3/4 of it had passed in build-up, and that the resolution was yet to be hinted at. You'd think that the end would feel rushed in this kind of a situation, but I didn't feel that way after everything was said and done. The resolution, while very different than what I thought would occur, fit the story very well, and left the reader an opening to extend the ending as they choose. <br /><br />Overall, I really liked this one, and I wouldn't hesitate to recommend it to someone looking for something enjoyable and interesting to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14950613501014098819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Robert Tabb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9600111-robert-tabb"><img alt="Robert Tabb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442473720p2/9600111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373495237?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Tabb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Tabb" href="/user/show/9600111-robert-tabb">Robert Tabb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423107514" href="/book/show/5990018-airman">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373495237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer451209432205953423">My wife mentioned the other day that I am "all about the ending" when it comes to books or movies. And that is why I can't bring myself to give Airman 5 stars even though it is one of the most enjoyable books I've read. <br/><br/>A royal romance, a plot to overthrow the government, a prison break, and high-flying (literally - of course everything in a book is literal) adventure, and awesome names (Declan Brokehart is such a cool name) abound in this wonderfully written adventure following Conor Brokehart'</span>
  <span id="freeText451209432205953423" style="display:none">My wife mentioned the other day that I am "all about the ending" when it comes to books or movies. And that is why I can't bring myself to give Airman 5 stars even though it is one of the most enjoyable books I've read. <br /><br />A royal romance, a plot to overthrow the government, a prison break, and high-flying (literally - of course everything in a book is literal) adventure, and awesome names (Declan Brokehart is such a cool name) abound in this wonderfully written adventure following Conor Brokehart's tale of tragedy and triumph. <br /><br />Colfer made me care about the characters and kept me turning pages. And while I wanted Conor to get out of trouble as quickly as possible, Colfer did a wonderful job of not rushing events or escapes. The good guys are good, the bad guys are bad, and the settings are cold and suitable for the plot to unfold. <br /><br />My only problem was that after being totally engrossed in the first 9/10 of the book the last bit left me going "that's how it wraps up?" I just wanted more from the ending. Otherwise Loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="451209432205953423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1358687694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1358687694" />
    <a title="Ezra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33213063-ezra"><img alt="Ezra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485153100p2/33213063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1358687694?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376351524" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376351524?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.E." class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.E." href="/user/show/60173003-j-e">J.E.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376351524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14277361135551118854">An inventive, imaginative story. Simple, but intelligent and emotionally complex. Good character development, even without getting very deep into the characters head. It started out very MG, and as the character grew the narrative grew a bit. But it never got to the point that I would consider it YA, even though the character was 17 at the end. <br/> I did have one small complaint, which is probably a manner of taste. (some spoilers) The text was very clear that the character's family was the main dr</span>
  <span id="freeText14277361135551118854" style="display:none">An inventive, imaginative story. Simple, but intelligent and emotionally complex. Good character development, even without getting very deep into the characters head. It started out very MG, and as the character grew the narrative grew a bit. But it never got to the point that I would consider it YA, even though the character was 17 at the end. <br /> I did have one small complaint, which is probably a manner of taste. (some spoilers) The text was very clear that the character's family was the main driving factor behind everything. The emotional damage he received from his father through the lies of the antagonist, and the love for his family that caused him to keep his distance for their safety even if they hated him. <br /> However, we only see maybe two paragraphs describing his revelation that his father had been lied to just as he had been, and the guilt of that moment. And no real resolution. But we get a whole chapter about the girl he liked, when their relationships as kids, sure, was great but it wasn't the focus of the book. I really would have liked to see some of the effects of the family. But, that was maybe a bit heavy for an MG novel, so I get why it wasn't included. <br /> Overall, it was a great book. A nice, straightforward read that gave me some great inspiration and kept me very involved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14277361135551118854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067631307" />
    <a title="Writer&#39;s Relief" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7400591-writer-s-relief"><img alt="Writer&#39;s Relief" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326489445p2/7400591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067631307?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Writer&#39;s Relief" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Writer&#39;s Relief" href="/user/show/7400591-writer-s-relief">Writer&#39;s Relief</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067631307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5306664980912836371">Imagine a mash-up of an Ironman graphic novel with The Count of Monte Cristo, and you have Eoin Colfer’s The Airman. The beginning of The Airman feels a little like a superhero origin story. Our young protagonist, Conor, is the son of a king’s guard, and he spends his time exploring the castle. We meet his childhood friend, the princess, and following along while he learns a crazy amount of skills from his wise and talented tutor—who happens to believe that someday humans will be able to fly the</span>
  <span id="freeText5306664980912836371" style="display:none">Imagine a mash-up of an Ironman graphic novel with The Count of Monte Cristo, and you have Eoin Colfer’s The Airman. The beginning of The Airman feels a little like a superhero origin story. Our young protagonist, Conor, is the son of a king’s guard, and he spends his time exploring the castle. We meet his childhood friend, the princess, and following along while he learns a crazy amount of skills from his wise and talented tutor—who happens to believe that someday humans will be able to fly the skies in heavier-than-air machines.<br /><br />Many years pass, and the king is murdered. Unfortunately Conor find himself caught up in the conspiracy and thrown in prison. His friends and family believe he’s dead. Eventually Conor meets some new friends, and he begins crafting an ingenious plan for revenge against those who have wronged him. His plan has to do with a flying machine.<br /><br />The ending did feel a little rushed, and details of the supporting cast were scant, but overall, The Airman was a wild ride and entertaining revenge adventure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5306664980912836371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1623686699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623686699" />
    <a title="Jamie Dacyczyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5407713-jamie-dacyczyn"><img alt="Jamie Dacyczyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306204362p2/5407713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623686699?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie Dacyczyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie Dacyczyn" href="/user/show/5407713-jamie-dacyczyn">Jamie Dacyczyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5407713-jamie-dacyczyn?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5407713-jamie-dacyczyn?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623686699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6148677741591594001">Well, I think I'll go ahead and give this one 4 stars, which is fairy high praise from me. I didn't care for Artemis Fowl when I read it years ago, but still decided to give this stand-alone novel a shot. Have I ever mentioned how much I LOVE stand-alone novels compared to fluffed trilogies or endless series?<br/><br/>This book felt a bit like a superhero origin tale. Although it was a bit far fetched in some areas (of course our young protagonist learns fencing, wrestling, AND karate from a master, how c</span>
  <span id="freeText6148677741591594001" style="display:none">Well, I think I'll go ahead and give this one 4 stars, which is fairy high praise from me. I didn't care for Artemis Fowl when I read it years ago, but still decided to give this stand-alone novel a shot. Have I ever mentioned how much I LOVE stand-alone novels compared to fluffed trilogies or endless series?<br /><br />This book felt a bit like a superhero origin tale. Although it was a bit far fetched in some areas (of course our young protagonist learns fencing, wrestling, AND karate from a master, how convenient), you just kind of go along with the ride for the sake of the adventure. I mean, it all COULD happen, it's just a bit unlikely. Suspend a little disbelief, and just look at it like that superhero origin. <br /><br />Another reviewer compared this to the Count of Monte Cristo mixed with Batman and/or Ironman. That seems about right. The son of a king's guard, Conor, spends his days exploring the royal castle with his childhood friend the princess, while learning insane amounts of skills from his ridiculously talented tutor who is also obsessed with the idea that humans could someday fly on heavier-than-air machines. Years later, the king is murdered, and as part of the conspiracy Conor is tossed into prison while his family and friends think he's dead. In prison, he makes some powerful friends, and also squirrels away some of the diamonds that he and his fellow prisoners are forced to mine for. A daring escape later, and Conor is able to set about plans to build flying machines and seek revenge.<br /><br />So yeah...very Monte Cristo, and very much like a steampunk Ironman. Again, there were some things that were quite far fetched, but that's fine. I do wish that the female characters (Conor's mother and Princess Isabella) had gotten more screentime and development, but I guess that's the problem with spending so much time imprisoned. The ending also felt a bit weak and abrupt, so for these things I'll detract a star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6148677741591594001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_595571332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595571332" />
    <a title="Penny McGill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7033258-penny-mcgill"><img alt="Penny McGill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353779762p2/7033258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/595571332?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny McGill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny McGill" href="/user/show/7033258-penny-mcgill">Penny McGill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7033258-penny-mcgill?shelf=for-older-kids">for-older-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595571332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8015174541411147799">We liked this book a lot - drawn to it by Eoin Colfer, of course - but I have to say I am a bit sorry that my 11-year old daughter read it. I know that is a bit crazy because she has done the Hunger Games, Maze Runner and Divergent and they are filled with violence and stress that I hope neither she or any of her friends ever deal with or even think they'll come close to seeing in their lives but the details in those series seem to be on the edge of entertainment, as if there isn't ever a chance</span>
  <span id="freeText8015174541411147799" style="display:none">We liked this book a lot - drawn to it by Eoin Colfer, of course - but I have to say I am a bit sorry that my 11-year old daughter read it. I know that is a bit crazy because she has done the Hunger Games, Maze Runner and Divergent and they are filled with violence and stress that I hope neither she or any of her friends ever deal with or even think they'll come close to seeing in their lives but the details in those series seem to be on the edge of entertainment, as if there isn't ever a chance that they could happen. With Airman it's not something that our generation of kids could experience but the way that Eoin writes the main character - Conor - is so compelling that it was hard NOT to believe that this was happening and hard not to keep thinking about his situation after we were finished our nightly reading (I actually read on through the book without her - not a good thing to admit but I really needed to see what was going to happen). <br /><br />Any description of the book would be too much of a spoiler for anyone but I will say that this would be a wonderful choice for an older boy and a fine option for someone who had enjoyed Kenneth Oppel's current books about Young Frankenstein. If I were talking with kids or parents in the library I would caution them that the level of violence and torture in a section of the book that deals with a prison is enough to cause a sensitive stomach to turn over a bit but the power of the story and the way that Eion Colfer approaches it is worth that burbling stomach. Not for younger kids, even if they have the reading level, it is a teen read for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8015174541411147799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66329937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66329937" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1966812-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288068457p2/1966812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66329937?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/1966812-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423107507" href="/book/show/749383.Airman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1966812-katherine?shelf=kid-s-books">kid-s-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66329937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4995648215929449651">I read this to my step-daughter. We had read Colfer’s previous books all of which we enjoyed, so we were looking forward to this one. It was a disappointment. <br/><br/>None of Eoin Colfer’s books are exactly realistic, in the Artemis Fowl series for instance, fairies, centaurs and wild, impossible schemes abound, but there’s a sense of fun, a playfulness that keeps the reader entertained and engaged. The Airman is serious, bleak even, so that there is nothing to balance the pure comic book evil of the vi</span>
  <span id="freeText4995648215929449651" style="display:none">I read this to my step-daughter. We had read Colfer’s previous books all of which we enjoyed, so we were looking forward to this one. It was a disappointment. <br /><br />None of Eoin Colfer’s books are exactly realistic, in the Artemis Fowl series for instance, fairies, centaurs and wild, impossible schemes abound, but there’s a sense of fun, a playfulness that keeps the reader entertained and engaged. The Airman is serious, bleak even, so that there is nothing to balance the pure comic book evil of the villains or the horrors that befall our hero beginning at the tender age of 14. There are occasional attempts to inject a little humour every now and then but for the most part they just fall flat and in our case were more likely to induce a shake of the head shake than giggles. <br /><br />As horrific as Connor‘s life becomes the feats he accomplishes are just as extreme. As much as I wanted him to succeed, I couldn’t help but roll my eyes as he defeats astounding odds time after time after time. Even if I could bring myself to suspend my disbelief long enough to accept Connor’s extreme intellectual and mechanical brilliance (augmented, of course with oodles of luck and fortuitous gusts of wind that seem to be forever coming out of nowhere) nothing could make me swallow the image of a severely injured, exhausted and frightened 14 year old boy defeating an experienced thug for hire in a one-on-one battle. <br /><br />And worst of all, the big, bad villain is presumed dead at the end. Presumed. And we all know what that means – sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4995648215929449651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1409230781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409230781" />
    <a title="Zara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28262919-zara"><img alt="Zara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483876507p2/28262919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409230781?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zara" href="/user/show/28262919-zara">Zara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141322216" href="/book/show/6333622-airman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=physical-copies-i-own">physical-copies-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409230781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4836853185027159791"><blockquote>
  <i>"Conor Broekhart was born to fly, or more accurately he was born flying."</i>
</blockquote><br/>I <b>enjoyed <i>Airman</i> much more the second time around</b>. <br/><br/>Conor Broekhart was born flying and has been obsessed with the idea of flight ever since. At the age of fourteen, he is labelled a traitor and sent to Little Saltee prison for a crime that he did not commit. The only way that he can escape the prison and reclaim his life is by flight.<br/><br/>Conor is an <b>extremely likable character</b>. He's intelligent and has a scientist's mind wh</span>
  <span id="freeText4836853185027159791" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Conor Broekhart was born to fly, or more accurately he was born flying."</i>
</blockquote><br />I <b>enjoyed <i>Airman</i> much more the second time around</b>. <br /><br />Conor Broekhart was born flying and has been obsessed with the idea of flight ever since. At the age of fourteen, he is labelled a traitor and sent to Little Saltee prison for a crime that he did not commit. The only way that he can escape the prison and reclaim his life is by flight.<br /><br />Conor is an <b>extremely likable character</b>. He's intelligent and has a scientist's mind which means that he's always planning his next idea or invention. Conor might be one of those <b>good-at-everything characters</b>, but <b>I didn't mind it</b> because <b>I wanted him to succeed</b>. <br /><br />The secondary characters are <b>quite unique</b>. Victor Vigny is Conor's teacher and is also a flight-obsessed scientist. Linus Wynter is a blind musician who befriends Conor in prison. Princess Isabella is Conor's childhood friend and crush and their <b>interactions are adorable</b>. I also <b>love Conor's parents</b>, Declan and Catherine. Marshall Hugo Bonvilain is <b>more villainous than a villain can be</b> (it's not like his name is a dead giveaway or anything). I prefer morally ambiguous characters, but since this book is on the younger side of the YA spectrum, <b>things are very black-and-white</b>. I <b>didn't mind it</b> because sometimes it's nice to read books where <b>there's a clear line between the heroes and the villains</b>. <br /><br />The <b>best part</b> of <i>Airman</i> is the <b>plot and pacing</b>. <i>Airman</i> has a <b>dash of everything</b>. There's adventure, science, romance, betrayal, inventions and prison escapes. <br /><br /><i>Airman</i> is a <b>gripping</b> and <b>delightful</b> alternate history story that pays tribute to the history of flight. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>"A monkey glances up and sees a banana, and that's as far as he looks. A visionary looks up and sees the moon." (Victor Vigny)</i>
</blockquote> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4836853185027159791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12880174607510538949">Like most of Eoin Colfer's work, Airman was delightful, engaging, and FUN to read. It doesn't seem to matter what subject or genre he's writing about, I am always enthralled by his characters and their stories. <br/><br/>My only nitpick about this story was towards the ending, so I'll try not to spoil it. The villain leaves a message for Conor that directly contradicts information he thought true, yet he never realizes it until he's told outright by others. Then again, the message wasn't relayed exactly a</span>
  <span id="freeText12880174607510538949" style="display:none">Like most of Eoin Colfer's work, Airman was delightful, engaging, and FUN to read. It doesn't seem to matter what subject or genre he's writing about, I am always enthralled by his characters and their stories. <br /><br />My only nitpick about this story was towards the ending, so I'll try not to spoil it. The villain leaves a message for Conor that directly contradicts information he thought true, yet he never realizes it until he's told outright by others. Then again, the message wasn't relayed exactly as dictated, but the crux was still there. I suppose I can forgive him this one, though.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Bonvilain leaves the message with Linus, he specifically says that the group will be having "a small dinner to celebrate the life of Conor Broekhart [...]. It will be the third anniversary of his death." Why would his parents and Isabella toast him if they thought him a traitor? However, Conor only hears from Linus that they are attending "a dinner for Conor Broekhart." Still, it seems obvious enough that they have all been fed different lies, yet Conor still thinks they hate him when he infiltrates the tower. Not a plot hole or anything egregious, just something I noticed and wondered why Conor didn't. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

    <a title="Sarah Cavar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4428746-sarah-cavar"><img alt="Sarah Cavar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515252891p2/4428746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2393588538?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Cavar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Cavar" href="/user/show/4428746-sarah-cavar">Sarah Cavar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4428746-sarah-cavar?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2393588538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14797895927668688113">3(.5) well-deserved stars for amazing storytelling and perfect pacing. It's a quick, escapist read, easy to get lost in. <br/><br/>-1.5 stars for its frustrating eurocentrism and uncritical use of so-called "period appropriate language" (such as "Oriental" instead of "Asian"), the way it denied agency to Isabella (one of only two women –– or as the book calls them, "females"–– in the book with speaking roles) when her intellect and independence clearly rivaled the male MC. <br/><br/>Also, this book does that thing </span>
  <span id="freeText14797895927668688113" style="display:none">3(.5) well-deserved stars for amazing storytelling and perfect pacing. It's a quick, escapist read, easy to get lost in. <br /><br />-1.5 stars for its frustrating eurocentrism and uncritical use of so-called "period appropriate language" (such as "Oriental" instead of "Asian"), the way it denied agency to Isabella (one of only two women –– or as the book calls them, "females"–– in the book with speaking roles) when her intellect and independence clearly rivaled the male MC. <br /><br />Also, this book does that thing with the "super-smart nerd boy is baffled by the femalez!!11!" trope that I am so very tired of. Lastly...there's a blind character in the book. There are a lot of cliched falsehoods about blindness in the book, like the notion that blind people all "just see darkness" and all have super-enhanced other senses. <br /><br />Engagement with Steampunk (as with many other genres) requires a suspension of disbelief. I wish Colfer had used his creativity to draw a Victorian-aethetiqued Steampunk work that wasn't so rife with unchallenged -isms. It's FICTION, after all! Try something new for once!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14797895927668688113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11316787151933886113">I thought this book was just really overwhelming in terms of historical accurateness even though it was a fiction novel. I really liked the plot how it kind of related to Icarus having to fly out of a prison cell in order to escape the tower he is trapped in. This novel is dark with lots of mystery, adventure, and sometimes a feel-good type of feeling. I thought that the book represented a lot of the past events in history like locking him up in a tower like they did Helen of Troy while other fa</span>
  <span id="freeText11316787151933886113" style="display:none">I thought this book was just really overwhelming in terms of historical accurateness even though it was a fiction novel. I really liked the plot how it kind of related to Icarus having to fly out of a prison cell in order to escape the tower he is trapped in. This novel is dark with lots of mystery, adventure, and sometimes a feel-good type of feeling. I thought that the book represented a lot of the past events in history like locking him up in a tower like they did Helen of Troy while other factions were down below fighting. One thing that I thought could've been done better was the character development. The main character seemed mostly static from beginning to end and the other supporting characters were just there with no real emotions or feelings that popped out. “A monkey glances up and sees a banana, and that's as far as he looks. A visionary looks up and sees the moon.” This was my favorite quote out of the entire novel and the moment I read it I knew I would be picking it for my review. I liked how it kind of put into perspective how the world is viewed by different people and how also it is full of opposing viewpoints and people. </span>
